|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|---------------|----------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
[Jakarta's cities/municipalities (*Kota Administratif*)]

The province comprises three of Indonesia's 84 national electoral districts to elect members to the [People's Representative Council](/wiki/Indonesian_Parliament "Indonesian Parliament"). The **Jakarta I Electoral District** consists of the administrative city of East Jakarta, and elects 6 members to the People's Representative Council. The **Jakarta II Electoral District** consists of the administrative cities of Central Jakarta and South Jskarta, together with all overseas voters, and elects 7 members to the People's Representative Council. The **Jakarta III Electoral District** consists of the administrative cities of North Jakarta and West Jakarta, together with the Thousand Islands Regency, and elects 8 members to the People's Representative Council.^[\[232\]](#cite_note-235)^{#cite_ref-235}  

Infrastructure {#Infrastructure}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Infrastructure")\]

To transform the city into a more liveable one, a ten-year *urban regeneration* project was undertaken, for Rp 571 trillion ($40.5 billion). The project aimed to develop infrastructure, including the creation of a better integrated public transit system and the improvement of the city's clean water and wastewater systems, housing, and flood control systems.^[\[233\]](#cite_note-236)^{#cite_ref-236}  

### Transportation {#Transportation}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Transportation")\]  
See also: [Greater Jakarta Integrated Mass Transit System](/wiki/Greater_Jakarta_Integrated_Mass_Transit_System "Greater Jakarta Integrated Mass Transit System")  
Main category: [Roads of Jakarta](/wiki/Category:Roads_of_Jakarta "Category:Roads of Jakarta")  
[![KRL](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Percobaan_205-10_dengan_Livery_KAI_Commuter_terbaru_Tahun_2020.jpg/170px-Percobaan_205-10_dengan_Livery_KAI_Commuter_terbaru_Tahun_2020.jpg)](/wiki/File:Percobaan_205-10_dengan_Livery_KAI_Commuter_terbaru_Tahun_2020.jpg)  
[![MRT](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Jakarta_MRT_TS11_leaving_Haji_Nawi_Station.jpg/170px-Jakarta_MRT_TS11_leaving_Haji_Nawi_Station.jpg)](/wiki/File:Jakarta_MRT_TS11_leaving_Haji_Nawi_Station.jpg)  
[![LRT](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/LRT_Jabodebek_Bekasi_Line.jpg/170px-LRT_Jabodebek_Bekasi_Line.jpg)](/wiki/File:LRT_Jabodebek_Bekasi_Line.jpg)  
[![Airport rail link](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Perubahan_Logo_pada_Lin_Soekarno-Hatta_MRI_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Perubahan_Logo_pada_Lin_Soekarno-Hatta_MRI_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Perubahan_Logo_pada_Lin_Soekarno-Hatta_MRI_(cropped).jpg)  
[![LRT](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/LRT_Jakarta_-_Hyundai_Rotem_LRV_in_Boulevard_Utara_Station.jpg/170px-LRT_Jakarta_-_Hyundai_Rotem_LRV_in_Boulevard_Utara_Station.jpg)](/wiki/File:LRT_Jakarta_-_Hyundai_Rotem_LRV_in_Boulevard_Utara_Station.jpg)  
[![BRT](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Transjakarta%2C_MYS-17066%2C_Scania_K310IB_6x2%2A4%2C_March_17th%2C_2019_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Transjakarta%2C_MYS-17066%2C_Scania_K310IB_6x2%2A4%2C_March_17th%2C_2019_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Transjakarta,_MYS-17066,_Scania_K310IB_6x2*4,_March_17th,_2019_(cropped).jpg)  
Various means of public transport in Jakarta; from top left to right: [KRL Commuterline](/wiki/KRL_Commuterline "KRL Commuterline"), [Jakarta MRT](/wiki/Jakarta_MRT "Jakarta MRT"), [Jabodebek LRT](/wiki/Jabodebek_LRT "Jabodebek LRT"), [Soekarno--Hatta Airport Rail Link](/wiki/Soekarno%E2%80%93Hatta_Airport_Rail_Link "Soekarno–Hatta Airport Rail Link"), [Jakarta LRT](/wiki/Jakarta_LRT "Jakarta LRT"), and [Transjakarta](/wiki/Transjakarta "Transjakarta")  
This section is an excerpt from [Transport in Jakarta](/wiki/Transport_in_Jakarta "Transport in Jakarta").\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Transport_in_Jakarta&action=edit)\]  
As a metropolitan area of about 30 million people, Jakarta has a variety of transport systems.^[\[234\]](#cite_note-Transport_in_Jakarta_NYT8413-237)^ Jakarta was awarded 2021 global [Sustainable Transport Award](/wiki/Sustainable_Transport_Award "Sustainable Transport Award") (STA) for integrated public transportation system.^[\[235\]](#cite_note-238)^{#cite_ref-238}

The city prioritized development of road networks, which were mostly designed to accommodate private vehicles.^[\[236\]](#cite_note-Transport_in_Jakarta_Easts.info-239)^ A notable feature of Jakarta's present road system is the [toll road](/wiki/Toll_road "Toll road") network. Composed of an [inner](/wiki/Jakarta_Inner_Ring_Road "Jakarta Inner Ring Road") and [outer](/wiki/Jakarta_Outer_Ring_Road "Jakarta Outer Ring Road") [ring road](/wiki/Ring_road "Ring road") and five toll roads radiating outwards, the network provides inner as well as outer city connections. An 'odd-even' policy limits road use to cars with either odd or even-numbered registration plates on a particular day as a transitional measure to alleviate traffic congestion until the future introduction of [electronic road pricing](/wiki/Electronic_road_pricing "Electronic road pricing").{#cite_ref-Transport_in_Jakarta_Easts.info_239-0}

There are many bus terminals in the city, from where buses operate on numerous routes to connect neighborhoods within the city limit, to other areas of [Greater Jakarta](/wiki/Jabodetabek "Jabodetabek") and to cities across the island of [Java](/wiki/Java "Java"). The biggest of the bus terminal is [Pulo Gebang Bus Terminal](/wiki/Pulo_Gebang_Bus_Terminal "Pulo Gebang Bus Terminal"), which is arguably the largest of its kind in Southeast Asia.^[\[237\]](#cite_note-Transport_in_Jakarta_bisnis.liputan6.com-240)^ Main terminus for long distance train services are [Gambir](/wiki/Gambir_railway_station "Gambir railway station") and [Pasar Senen](/wiki/Pasar_Senen_railway_station "Pasar Senen railway station"). [Whoosh High-speed railways](/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Indonesia "High-speed rail in Indonesia") is connecting Jakarta to [Bandung](/wiki/Bandung "Bandung") and another one is at the planning stage from Jakarta to [Surabaya](/wiki/Surabaya "Surabaya").{#cite_ref-Transport_in_Jakarta_bisnis.liputan6.com_240-0}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Halte_CSW.jpg/170px-Halte_CSW.jpg)](/wiki/File:Halte_CSW.jpg) A skybridge at [CSW-ASEAN TOD](/wiki/CSW-ASEAN_TOD "CSW-ASEAN TOD")

As of September 2023, Jakarta's public transport service coverage has reached 86 percent, which is targeted to increase to 95 percent. Rapid transit in [Greater Jakarta](/wiki/Greater_Jakarta_Area "Greater Jakarta Area") consists of [TransJakarta](/wiki/TransJakarta "TransJakarta") bus rapid transit, [Jakarta LRT](/wiki/Jakarta_LRT "Jakarta LRT"), [Jakarta MRT](/wiki/Jakarta_MRT "Jakarta MRT"), [KRL Commuterline](/wiki/KRL_Commuterline "KRL Commuterline"), [Jabodebek LRT](/wiki/Jabodebek_LRT "Jabodebek LRT"), and [Soekarno-Hatta Airport Rail Link](/wiki/Soekarno-Hatta_Airport_Rail_Link "Soekarno-Hatta Airport Rail Link"). The city administration is building transit oriented development like [Dukuh Atas TOD](/wiki/Dukuh_Atas_TOD "Dukuh Atas TOD") and [CSW-ASEAN TOD](/wiki/CSW-ASEAN_TOD "CSW-ASEAN TOD") in several area across Jakarta to facilitate commuters to transfer between different mode of public transportation.

Privately owned bus systems like [Kopaja](/wiki/Kopaja "Kopaja"), [MetroMini](/wiki/MetroMini,_Jakarta "MetroMini, Jakarta"), [Mayasari Bakti](https://id.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mayasari_Bakti "id:Mayasari Bakti") and [PPD](/wiki/Pengangkutan_Penumpang_Djakarta "Pengangkutan Penumpang Djakarta") also provide important services for Jakarta commuters with numerous routes throughout the city, many routes are/will replaced/replaced by [Minitrans](/wiki/Minitrans "Minitrans") and [Metrotrans](/wiki/Metrotrans "Metrotrans") buses.^[\[238\]](#cite_note-241)^ [Pedicabs](/wiki/Pedicab "Pedicab") are banned from the city for causing traffic congestion. [Bajaj](/wiki/Auto_rickshaw#Indonesia "Auto rickshaw") auto rickshaw provide local transportation in the back streets of some parts of the city. [Angkot](/wiki/Angkot "Angkot") microbuses also play a major role in road transport of Jakarta. [Taxicabs](/wiki/Taxicab "Taxicab") and [ojeks](/wiki/Motorcycle_taxi#Indonesia "Motorcycle taxi") (motorcycle taxis) are available in the city. As of January 2023, about 2.6 million people use public transportation daily in Jakarta.^[\[239\]](#cite_note-242)^{#cite_ref-242}

The city administration has undertaken a project to build about 500 kilometers of [bicycle](/wiki/Bicycle "Bicycle") lanes. As of June 2021, Jakarta already has 63 kilometers of bicycle lanes, and another 101 kilometers will be added by the end of the year 2021.^[\[240\]](#cite_note-243)^^[\[241\]](#cite_note-244)^{#cite_ref-244}

[Soekarno--Hatta International Airport](/wiki/Soekarno%E2%80%93Hatta_International_Airport "Soekarno–Hatta International Airport") (CGK) is the main [airport](/wiki/Airport "Airport") serving the Greater Jakarta area, while [Halim Perdanakusuma Airport](/wiki/Halim_Perdanakusuma_Airport "Halim Perdanakusuma Airport") (HLP) accommodates private and [low-cost](/wiki/Low-cost_carrier "Low-cost carrier") [domestic flights](/wiki/Domestic_flight "Domestic flight"). Other airports in the [Jakarta metropolitan area](/wiki/Jakarta_metropolitan_area "Jakarta metropolitan area") include [Pondok Cabe Airport](/wiki/Pondok_Cabe_Airport "Pondok Cabe Airport") and an airfield on Pulau Panjang, part of the [Thousand Island archipelago](/wiki/Thousand_Islands_(Indonesia) "Thousand Islands (Indonesia)").

Indonesia's busiest and Jakarta's main seaport [Tanjung Priok](/wiki/Port_of_Tanjung_Priok "Port of Tanjung Priok") serves many ferry connections to different parts of Indonesia. The old port [Sunda Kelapa](/wiki/Sunda_Kelapa "Sunda Kelapa") only accommodate [pinisi](/wiki/Pinisi "Pinisi"), a traditional two-masted wooden sailing ship serving inter-island freight service in the archipelago. [Muara Angke](/wiki/Muara_Angke "Muara Angke") is used as a public port to [Thousand Islands](/wiki/Thousand_Islands_(Indonesia) "Thousand Islands (Indonesia)"), while Marina [Ancol](/wiki/Ancol "Ancol") is used as a tourist port.^[\[242\]](#cite_note-245)^{#cite_ref-245}

For payment method in public transportation (for KAI Commuter line, TransJakarta, LRT Jakarta, LRT Jabodebek, MRT Jakarta) already using cashless. Travelers can use Electronic money banking cards. The electronic money cards include those issued, namely:

* BRIZZI (issued by Bank BRI)
* TapCash (issued by Bank BNI)
* e-Money (issued by Bank Mandiri)
* Flazz (issued by Bank BCA)
* Jakcard (issued by Bank DKI)

The electronic banking cards is integrated cad can be accepted in KAI Commuter line, TransJakarta, LRT Jakarta, LRT Jabodebek, MRT Jakarta, eToll payment and parking payment. The electronic bank card can be bought in Bank Branch office or in e-commerce.

For the electronic banking card Top Up can be done at:

* Indomaret Outlet (convenient store).
* Alfamart Outlet (convenient store).
* Alfamidi Outlet (convenient store).
* Bright Store Outlet (convenient store).
* e-Money Card Vending Machine.

Jakarta is part of the Maritime [Silk Road](/wiki/Silk_Road "Silk Road") that runs from the Chinese coast via the [Suez Canal](/wiki/Suez_Canal "Suez Canal") to the Mediterranean and there to the Upper Adriatic region.^[\[243\]](#cite_note-246)^^[\[244\]](#cite_note-247)^^[\[245\]](#cite_note-248)^  

### Healthcare {#Healthcare}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Healthcare")\]

Jakarta has many of the country's best-equipped private and public [healthcare facilities](/wiki/Healthcare_in_Indonesia "Healthcare in Indonesia"). In 2012, the Governor of Jakarta [Joko Widodo](/wiki/Joko_Widodo "Joko Widodo") introduced a [universal health care](/wiki/Universal_health_care "Universal health care") program, the 'Healthy Jakarta Card' (*Kartu Jakarta Sehat* , KJS).^[\[246\]](#cite_note-249)^ In January 2014, the Indonesian government launched a universal health care system called the *[Jaminan Kesehatan Nasional](/wiki/Jaminan_Kesehatan_Nasional "Jaminan Kesehatan Nasional")* (JKN), which is run by [BPJS Kesehatan](/wiki/BPJS_Kesehatan "BPJS Kesehatan").^[\[247\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBritnell201547-250)^ KJS integrated into JKN,^[\[248\]](#cite_note-251)^ and KJS cards were valid till 2018.^[\[249\]](#cite_note-252)^ As of 2021, 85.55% of the people of Jakarta is covered by JKN.^[\[250\]](#cite_note-253)^{#cite_ref-253}

Government-run hospitals are of a good standard but are often overcrowded. Government-run specialised hospitals include [Dr. Cipto Mangunkusumo Hospital](/wiki/Dr._Cipto_Mangunkusumo_Hospital "Dr. Cipto Mangunkusumo Hospital"), [Gatot Soebroto Army Hospital](/wiki/Gatot_Soebroto_Army_Hospital "Gatot Soebroto Army Hospital"), as well as community hospitals and [puskesmas](/wiki/Puskesmas "Puskesmas"). Other options for healthcare services include private hospitals and clinics. The private healthcare sector has seen significant changes since the government began allowing foreign investment in the private sector in 2010. While some private facilities are run by nonprofit or religious organisations, most are for-profit. Hospital chains such as [Siloam](/wiki/Siloam_Hospitals "Siloam Hospitals"), Pondok Indah Hospital Group, Mayapada, Mitra Keluarga, Medika, Medistra, Ciputra, Radjak Hospital Group, RS Bunda Group, and [Hermina](/wiki/Hermina_Hospitals "Hermina Hospitals") operate in the city.^[\[251\]](#cite_note-254)^^[\[252\]](#cite_note-255)^^[\[253\]](#cite_note-256)^{#cite_ref-256}  

### Water supply {#Water_supply}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Water supply")\]  
Further information: [Water privatisation in Jakarta](/wiki/Water_privatisation_in_Jakarta "Water privatisation in Jakarta")

Two private companies, PALYJA and Aetra, provide piped water in the western and eastern half of Jakarta respectively under 25-year concession contracts signed in 1998. A public asset holding company called PAM Jaya owns the infrastructure. Eighty per cent of the water distributed in Jakarta comes through the West Tarum Canal system from Jatiluhur reservoir on the [Citarum River](/wiki/Citarum_River "Citarum River"), 70 km (43 mi) southeast of the city. The water supply was privatised by President Suharto in 1998 to the French company [Suez Environnement](/wiki/Suez_Environnement "Suez Environnement") and the British company [Thames Water](/wiki/Thames_Water "Thames Water") International. Both companies subsequently sold their concessions to Indonesian companies. Customer growth in the first seven years of the concessions had been lower than before, possibly because of substantial inflation-adjusted tariff increases during this period. In 2005, tariffs were frozen, leading private water companies to cut down on investments.

According to PALYJA, the service coverage ratio increased substantially from 34% (1998) to 65% (2010) in the western half of the concession.^[\[254\]](#cite_note-257)^ According to data by the Jakarta Water Supply Regulatory Body, access in the eastern half of the city served by PTJ increased from about 57% in 1998 to about 67% in 2004 but stagnated afterward.^[\[255\]](#cite_note-258)^ However, other sources cite much lower access figures for piped water supply to houses, excluding access provided through public hydrants: one study estimated access as low as 25% in 2005,^[\[256\]](#cite_note-259)^ while another estimated it to be as low as 18.5% in 2011.^[\[257\]](#cite_note-260)^ Those without access to piped water get water mostly from wells that are often salty and unsanitary. As of 2017, according to the [Ministry of Energy and Mineral Resources](/wiki/Ministry_of_Energy_and_Mineral_Resources_(Indonesia) "Ministry of Energy and Mineral Resources (Indonesia)"), Jakarta had a crisis over clean water.^[\[258\]](#cite_note-261)^{#cite_ref-261}  

International relations {#International_relations}
--------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: International relations")\]  
See also: [List of diplomatic missions in Jakarta](/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_Jakarta "List of diplomatic missions in Jakarta")  

### International organisations {#International_organisations}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: International organisations")\]

Jakarta hosts foreign [embassies](/wiki/Diplomatic_mission "Diplomatic mission"). Jakarta also serves as the seat of [Association of Southeast Asian Nations](/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations "Association of Southeast Asian Nations") (ASEAN) Headquarters and is ASEAN's diplomatic capital.^[\[259\]](#cite_note-262)^{#cite_ref-262}

Jakarta is a member of the [Asian Network of Major Cities 21](/wiki/Asian_Network_of_Major_Cities_21 "Asian Network of Major Cities 21"), [C40 Cities Climate Leadership Group](/wiki/C40_Cities_Climate_Leadership_Group "C40 Cities Climate Leadership Group") and [ASEAN Smart Cities Network](/wiki/ASEAN_Smart_Cities_Network "ASEAN Smart Cities Network").  

### Twin towns -- sister cities {#Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Twin towns – sister cities")\]  
See also: [List of twin towns and sister cities in Indonesia](/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Indonesia "List of twin towns and sister cities in Indonesia")

Jakarta signed [sister city](/wiki/Sister_city "Sister city") agreements with other cities, including [Casablanca](/wiki/Casablanca "Casablanca"). To promote friendship between the two cities, the main avenue famous for its shopping and business centres was named after Jakarta's Moroccan sister city. No street in Casablanca is named after Jakarta. However, the Moroccan capital city of Rabat has an avenue named after [Sukarno](/wiki/Sukarno "Sukarno"), Indonesia's first president, to commemorate his visit in 1960 and as a token of friendship.^[\[260\]](#cite_note-JakartaPost2-263)^{#cite_ref-JakartaPost2_263-0}

Jakarta's sister cities are:^[\[261\]](#cite_note-sisters-264)^{#cite_ref-sisters_264-0}  
* [![Brunei](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Brunei.svg/23px-Flag_of_Brunei.svg.png)](/wiki/Brunei "Brunei") [Bandar Seri Begawan](/wiki/Bandar_Seri_Begawan "Bandar Seri Begawan"), Brunei
* [![Thailand](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/23px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png)](/wiki/Thailand "Thailand") [Bangkok](/wiki/Bangkok "Bangkok"), Thailand
* [![China](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png)](/wiki/China "China") [Beijing](/wiki/Beijing "Beijing"), China
* [![Germany](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png)](/wiki/Germany "Germany") [Berlin](/wiki/Berlin "Berlin"), Germany
* [![Morocco](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Morocco.svg/23px-Flag_of_Morocco.svg.png)](/wiki/Morocco "Morocco") [Casablanca](/wiki/Casablanca "Casablanca"), Morocco
* [![Palestine](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Palestine.svg/23px-Flag_of_Palestine.svg.png)](/wiki/Palestine "Palestine") [East Jerusalem](/wiki/East_Jerusalem "East Jerusalem"), Palestine
* [![Vietnam](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Vietnam.svg/23px-Flag_of_Vietnam.svg.png)](/wiki/Vietnam "Vietnam") [Hanoi](/wiki/Hanoi "Hanoi"), Vietnam
* [![Pakistan](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png)](/wiki/Pakistan "Pakistan") [Islamabad](/wiki/Islamabad "Islamabad"), Pakistan
* [![Turkey](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png)](/wiki/Turkey "Turkey") [Istanbul](/wiki/Istanbul "Istanbul"), Turkey
* [![Saudi Arabia](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png)](/wiki/Saudi_Arabia "Saudi Arabia") [Jeddah](/wiki/Jeddah "Jeddah"), Saudi Arabia
* [![Ukraine](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png)](/wiki/Ukraine "Ukraine") [Kyiv](/wiki/Kyiv "Kyiv"), Ukraine
* [![United States](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png)](/wiki/United_States "United States") [Los Angeles](/wiki/Los_Angeles "Los Angeles"), United States
* [![Philippines](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg.png)](/wiki/Philippines "Philippines") [Manila](/wiki/Manila "Manila"), Philippines
* [![Mozambique](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Flag_of_Mozambique.svg/23px-Flag_of_Mozambique.svg.png)](/wiki/Mozambique "Mozambique") [Maputo](/wiki/Maputo "Maputo"), Mozambique
* [![Russia](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png)](/wiki/Russia "Russia") [Moscow](/wiki/Moscow "Moscow"), Russia
* [![India](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/23px-Flag_of_India.svg.png)](/wiki/India "India") [Mumbai](/wiki/Mumbai "Mumbai"), India

### Cooperation and friendship {#Cooperation_and_friendship}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Cooperation and friendship")\]

Jakarta has established a partnership with [Rotterdam](/wiki/Rotterdam "Rotterdam"), especially on integrated urban water management, including capacity-building and knowledge exchange.^[\[262\]](#cite_note-NESO-265)^ This cooperation is mainly because both cities are dealing with similar problems; they lie in low-lying flat plains and are prone to flooding. Additionally, they have both implemented drainage systems involving canals, dams and pumps vital for both cities for below-sea-level areas.{#cite_ref-NESO_265-0}

In addition to its sister cities, Jakarta cooperates with:^[\[261\]](#cite_note-sisters-264)^{#cite_ref-sisters_264-1}

* [![United States](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png)](/wiki/United_States "United States") [Arkansas](/wiki/Arkansas "Arkansas"), United States
* [![Hungary](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/23px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png)](/wiki/Hungary "Hungary") [Budapest](/wiki/Budapest "Budapest"), Hungary
* [![Australia](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png)](/wiki/Australia "Australia") [New South Wales](/wiki/New_South_Wales "New South Wales"), Australia
* [![France](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png)](/wiki/France "France") [Paris](/wiki/Paris "Paris"), France
* [![Netherlands](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png)](/wiki/Netherlands "Netherlands") [Rotterdam](/wiki/Rotterdam "Rotterdam"), Netherlands
